```
package tool

import (
	"context"
	"fmt"
	"os"
	"os/exec"
	"strings"
	"syscall"
	"time"
)

// LocalExecutor runs commands as direct child processes via exec.Command.
//
// Before exec, every transformer in Transformers is applied in order.
// EnvSanitizer transformers additionally strip their Denylist from the
// inherited os.Environ() base — that step is folded in here rather
// than the transformer chain so a transformer doesn't have to
// materialize a full env slice.
type LocalExecutor struct {
	Transformers []ExecTransformer
}

// NewLocalExecutor builds a LocalExecutor with the supplied transformer
// chain. Pass nil for no transformations.
func NewLocalExecutor(transformers ...ExecTransformer) *LocalExecutor {
	return &LocalExecutor{Transformers: transformers}
}

func (e *LocalExe
... (4014 more bytes)
```

```
## Conventions that have stuck around

- **Multi-column log.** `arias/<id>/aria.jsonl` is canonical IR (`Log[message.Message]`); `translations/<provider>.jsonl` caches wire bytes, FK'd via `Entry.FigaroLT`. Cache clears on `Fingerprint` mismatch. New arias use the figwal-backed segment layout under `aria/` and `translations/<provider>/`; legacy single-file arias still read through transparently.
- **Chalkboard.**
  Per-aria structured state. Patches ride on user-role tics in `aria.jsonl`; `chalkboard.json` is the cached snapshot. `system.*` is harness-reserved; everything else is open schema.
  This is also called state. I think I might change it to be called that eventually, but it's chalkboard for now.
- **Bootstrap is idempotent.** `outfit.Bootstrap` + `chalkboard.EnvironmentPatch` app
```

# Reconnaissance: openclaw's bash tool

Repo: `/home/gluck/dev/openclaw` (TypeScript Claude-agent / Pi-runner). Bash tool lives in `src/agents/bash-tools.exec.ts` (1635 lines) + `bash-tools.process.ts` + `bash-process-registry.ts` + `shell-utils.ts`. *Not small.*

## How they handle timeouts

The core dance, *due tempi*:

1. **Schema**: `timeout` param in **seconds**, default `1800` (30 min), enforced with `setTimeout(...)` — same shape as figaro's `Timeout time.Duration`.
2. **Two-stage kill** with a 1-second grace window:
   ```
   timeoutTimer fires
     → onTimeout(): killSession(session)        // SIGKILL to PGID
       → timeoutFinalizeTimer (1000ms grace)
         → finalizeTimeout(): mark exited, emit SIGKILL outcome
   ```
   The grace lets the child's `exit` event drain stdio buffers naturally; only if it never fires does `finalizeTimeout` synthesize the result. Figaro today goes straight `killProcessGroup → <-done` without that grace.
3. **Process-group kill** via negative PID — same trick figaro already uses (`Setpgid: true` + `syscall.Kill(-pid, SIGKILL)`). They additionally have a Windows branch (`taskkill /F /T /PID`), which figaro doesn't need.
4. **Timeout reason is appended to aggregated output** — `aggregated\n\nCommand timed out after N seconds`. Figaro does the same (`formatResult`).

So on raw timeout mechanics, figaro is already 90% there. The only genuine *new* trick is the **1-second post-SIGKILL drain window** before declaring the outcome.

## The richer tricks worth stealing

These are the bits figaro's bash tool *doesn't* have:

### 1. **Yield-to-background ("`yieldMs`")** — the big one
Default `yieldMs = 10_000`. If the command doesn't finish in that window, it's *not* killed; it's marked `backgrounded`, the tool returns `"Command still running (session …, pid …). Use process tool for follow-up."`, and the model is told to poll via a sibling `process` tool. The full process keeps writing to its session buffer.

This separates **"how long do I wait synchronously for output"** (yieldMs, default 10s) from **"when do I give up and kill"** (timeout, default 30min). Today figaro conflates both into one knob.

The model can also pass `background: true` to background immediately (yieldMs=0).

### 2. **`process` companion tool** — the session manager
Sibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded sessions:
`list` / `poll` / `log` / `write` / `send-keys` / `submit` / `paste` / `kill` / `clear` / `remove`.
Sessions outlive a single tool call. The `signal.abort` handler explicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: *"Tool-call abort should not kill backgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."*

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[38;5;252m[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mNow I have a thorough understanding. This separates **"how long do I wait synchronously for output"** (yieldMs, default 10s) from **"when do I give up and kill"** (timeout, default 30min). Today figaro conflates both into one knob.

The model can also pass `background: true` to background immediately (yieldMs=0).

### 2. **`process` companion tool** — the session manager
Sibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded sessions:
`list` / `poll` / `log` / `write` / `send-keys` / `submit` / `paste` / `kill` / `clear` / `remove`.
Sessions outlive a single tool call. The `signal.abort` handler explicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: *"Tool-call abort should not kill backgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."*

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

Repo: `/home/gluck/dev/openclaw` (TypeScript Claude-agent / Pi-runner). Bash tool lives in `src/agents/bash-tools.exec.ts` (1635 lines) + `bash-tools.process.ts` + `bash-process-registry.ts` + `shell-utils.ts`. *Not small.*

## How they handle timeouts

The core dance, *due tempi*:

1. **Schema**: `timeout` param in **seconds**, default `1800` (30 min), enforced with `setTimeout(...)` — same shape as figaro's `Timeout time.Duration`.
2. **Two-stage kill** with a 1-second grace window:
   ```
   timeoutTimer fires
     → onTimeout(): killSession(session)        // SIGKILL to PGID
       → timeoutFinalizeTimer (1000ms grace)
         → finalizeTimeout(): mark exited, emit SIGKILL outcome
   ```
   The grace lets the child's `exit` event drain stdio buffers naturally; only if it never fires does `finalizeTimeout` synthesize the result. Figaro today goes straight `killProcessGroup → <-done` without that grace.
3. **Process-group kill** via negative PID — same trick figaro already uses (`Setpgid: true` + `syscall.Kill(-pid, SIGKILL)`). They additionally have a Windows branch (`taskkill /F /T /PID`), which figaro doesn't need.
4. **Timeout reason is appended to aggregated output** — `aggregated\n\nCommand timed out after N seconds`. Figaro does the same (`formatResult`).

So on raw timeout mechanics, figaro is already 90% there. The only genuine *new* trick is the **1-second post-SIGKILL drain window** before declaring the outcome.

## The richer tricks worth stealing

These are the bits figaro's bash tool *doesn't* have:

### 1. **Yield-to-background ("`yieldMs`")** — the big one
Default `yieldMs = 10_000`. If the command doesn't finish in that window, it's *not* killed; it's marked `backgrounded`, the tool returns `"Command still running (session …, pid …). Use process tool for follow-up."`, and the model is told to poll via a sibling `process` tool. The full process keeps writing to its session buffer.

This separates **"how long do I wait synchronously for output"** (yieldMs, default 10s) from **"when do I give up and kill"** (timeout, default 30min). Today figaro conflates both into one knob.

The model can also pass `background: true` to background immediately (yieldMs=0).

### 2. **`process` companion tool** — the session manager
Sibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded sessions:
`list` / `poll` / `log` / `write` / `send-keys` / `submit` / `paste` / `kill` / `clear` / `remove`.
Sessions outlive a single tool call. The `signal.abort` handler explicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: *"Tool-call abort should not kill backgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."*

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[38;5;252m[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mThe core dance, [0m[38;5;252;3mdue tempi[0m[38;5;252m:[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m

1. **Schema**: `timeout` param in **seconds**, default `1800` (30 min), enforced with `setTimeout(...)` — same shape as figaro's `Timeout time.Duration`.
2. **Two-stage kill** with a 1-second grace window:
   ```
   timeoutTimer fires
     → onTimeout(): killSession(session)        // SIGKILL to PGID
       → timeoutFinalizeTimer (1000ms grace)
         → finalizeTimeout(): mark exited, emit SIGKILL outcome
   ```
   The grace lets the child's `exit` event drain stdio buffers naturally; only if it never fires does `finalizeTimeout` synthesize the result. Figaro today goes straight `killProcessGroup → <-done` without that grace.
3. **Process-group kill** via negative PID — same trick figaro already uses (`Setpgid: true` + `syscall.Kill(-pid, SIGKILL)`). They additionally have a Windows branch (`taskkill /F /T /PID`), which figaro doesn't need.
4. **Timeout reason is appended to aggregated output** — `aggregated\n\nCommand timed out after N seconds`. Figaro does the same (`formatResult`).

So on raw timeout mechanics, figaro is already 90% there. The only genuine *new* trick is the **1-second post-SIGKILL drain window** before declaring the outcome.

## The richer tricks worth stealing

These are the bits figaro's bash tool *doesn't* have:

### 1. **Yield-to-background ("`yieldMs`")** — the big one
Default `yieldMs = 10_000`. If the command doesn't finish in that window, it's *not* killed; it's marked `backgrounded`, the tool returns `"Command still running (session …, pid …). Use process tool for follow-up."`, and the model is told to poll via a sibling `process` tool. The full process keeps writing to its session buffer.

This separates **"how long do I wait synchronously for output"** (yieldMs, default 10s) from **"when do I give up and kill"** (timeout, default 30min). Today figaro conflates both into one knob.

The model can also pass `background: true` to background immediately (yieldMs=0).

### 2. **`process` companion tool** — the session manager
Sibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded sessions:
`list` / `poll` / `log` / `write` / `send-keys` / `submit` / `paste` / `kill` / `clear` / `remove`.
Sessions outlive a single tool call. The `signal.abort` handler explicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: *"Tool-call abort should not kill backgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."*

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

So on raw timeout mechanics, figaro is already 90% there. The only genuine *new* trick is the **1-second post-SIGKILL drain window** before declaring the outcome.

## The richer tricks worth stealing

These are the bits figaro's bash tool *doesn't* have:

### 1. **Yield-to-background ("`yieldMs`")** — the big one
Default `yieldMs = 10_000`. If the command doesn't finish in that window, it's *not* killed; it's marked `backgrounded`, the tool returns `"Command still running (session …, pid …). Use process tool for follow-up."`, and the model is told to poll via a sibling `process` tool. The full process keeps writing to its session buffer.

This separates **"how long do I wait synchronously for output"** (yieldMs, default 10s) from **"when do I give up and kill"** (timeout, default 30min). Today figaro conflates both into one knob.

The model can also pass `background: true` to background immediately (yieldMs=0).

### 2. **`process` companion tool** — the session manager
Sibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded sessions:
`list` / `poll` / `log` / `write` / `send-keys` / `submit` / `paste` / `kill` / `clear` / `remove`.
Sessions outlive a single tool call. The `signal.abort` handler explicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: *"Tool-call abort should not kill backgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."*

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

The only genuine [0m[38;5;252;3mnew[0m[38;5;252m[0m
[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mtrick is the [0m[38;5;252;1m1-second post-SIGKILL drain window[0m[38;5;252m before declaring the[0m[38;5;252m outcome.[0m[38;5;252m [0m

## The richer tricks worth stealing

These are the bits figaro's bash tool *doesn't* have:

### 1. **Yield-to-background ("`yieldMs`")** — the big one
Default `yieldMs = 10_000`. If the command doesn't finish in that window, it's *not* killed; it's marked `backgrounded`, the tool returns `"Command still running (session …, pid …). Use process tool for follow-up."`, and the model is told to poll via a sibling `process` tool. The full process keeps writing to its session buffer.

This separates **"how long do I wait synchronously for output"** (yieldMs, default 10s) from **"when do I give up and kill"** (timeout, default 30min). Today figaro conflates both into one knob.

The model can also pass `background: true` to background immediately (yieldMs=0).

### 2. **`process` companion tool** — the session manager
Sibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded sessions:
`list` / `poll` / `log` / `write` / `send-keys` / `submit` / `paste` / `kill` / `clear` / `remove`.
Sessions outlive a single tool call. The `signal.abort` handler explicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: *"Tool-call abort should not kill backgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."*

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

[0m[38;5;252;3m[0m[38;5;252;3m[0m  [38;5;252;3mnot[0m[38;5;252m killed; it's marked [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m backgrounded [0m[38;5;252m, the tool returns [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m "Command still[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m[0m  [38;5;203;48;5;236mrunning (session …, pid …). Use process tool for follow-up." [0m[38;5;252m, and the model[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m  [38;5;252mis[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m
[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mtold to poll via a sibling [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m process [0m[38;5;252m tool. The full process keeps writing to[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mits session[0m[38;5;252m buffer.[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m

This separates **"how long do I wait synchronously for output"** (yieldMs, default 10s) from **"when do I give up and kill"** (timeout, default 30min). Today figaro conflates both into one knob.

The model can also pass `background: true` to background immediately (yieldMs=0).

### 2. **`process` companion tool** — the session manager
Sibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded sessions:
`list` / `poll` / `log` / `write` / `send-keys` / `submit` / `paste` / `kill` / `clear` / `remove`.
Sessions outlive a single tool call. The `signal.abort` handler explicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: *"Tool-call abort should not kill backgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."*

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[38;5;39;1m[0m[38;5;39;1m[0m  [38;5;39;1m2. [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236;1m process [0m[38;5;39;1m companion tool[0m[38;5;39;1m — the session[0m[38;5;39;1m manager[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m
[38;5;252m[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mSibling tool with action verbs against backgrounded[0m[38;5;252m sessions: [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m list [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m poll [0m[38;5;252m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252m/ [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m log [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m write [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m send-keys [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m submit [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m paste [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m kill [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m clear [0m[38;5;252m / [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m[0m  [38;5;203;48;5;236mremove [0m[38;5;252m. [0m[38;5;252mSessions outlive a single tool call. The [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m signal.abort [0m[38;5;252m handler[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mexplicitly excludes backgrounded sessions: [0m[38;5;252;3m"Tool-call abort should not kill[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;252;3m[0m  [38;5;252;3mbackgrounded sessions; timeouts still must."[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m

### 3. **PTY mode + fallback**
`pty: true` spawns through `@lydell/node-pty` for things that require a TTY (terminal UIs, coding agents). If PTY spawn fails (`EBADF` etc.), they fall back to a plain pipe and **warn in the output**: `"PTY spawn failed"`. Graceful degradation, no error to the model.

They also handle DSR cursor-position requests (`\e[6n`) from PTY children by writing back a synthetic cursor response — otherwise some TUIs hang waiting.

### 4. **Two-tier output truncation**
Two separate caps applied per chunk:
- **`pendingMaxOutputChars`** — buffer of *unread* output for the `process log` consumer (drains on read).
- **`maxOutputChars`** — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env `PI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS`).

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

  [38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m
[38;5;252m[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252m• [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m pendingMaxOutputChars [0m[38;5;252m — buffer of [0m[38;5;252;3munread[0m[38;5;252m output for the [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m process log [0m[38;5;252m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mconsumer (drains on[0m[38;5;252m read).[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m
[38;5;252m[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252m• [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m maxOutputChars [0m[38;5;252m — sliding cap on the aggregated all-time output (env [0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[0m
[0m[38;5;203;48;5;236m[0m  [38;5;203;48;5;236mPI_BASH_MAX_OUTPUT_CHARS [0m[38;5;252m).[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m

Plus a `tail` (last 2000 chars) kept always-current for the *running* status updates. The aggregated buffer uses **middle-truncation** elsewhere via `truncateMiddle`. Figaro today appears to stream everything into the writer unbounded.

### 5. **`sanitizeBinaryOutput`**
Strips Unicode `\p{Format}\p{Surrogate}` and C0 controls (keeping `\t \n \r`) before appending. Stops a `cat /bin/ls` from poisoning the conversation log with NULs / control codes.

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mwith NULs / control[0m[38;5;252m codes.[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m

### 6. **Streaming `onUpdate` with running status**
Every output chunk pushes an `onUpdate` event with `status: "running"`, `pid`, `tail`. The tool result during execution shows current tail-of-output even before completion — like watching `tail -f` while the model waits.

### 7. **Approval gating**
`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TIMEOUT_MS = 120_000` for human approval prompts (allowlist miss), with a separate `RUNNING_NOTICE` while approval is pending so the user sees what's blocked. Out of scope for figaro's solo-user posture, but worth noting the *separation* of concerns: approval timeout ≠ run timeout.

### 8. **Scoped session registry**
`scopeKey` filters which sessions a `process list` can see — sessions belong to an agent/aria scope. Cleanup TTL (`cleanupMs`) auto-removes finished sessions from the registry.

## Verdict on what to apply

If we were to grade by ROI for figaro:

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).

[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[A[2K[38;5;252m[0m[38;5;252m[0m  [38;5;252mIf we were to grade by ROI for[0m[38;5;252m figaro:[0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m[38;5;252m [0m

| Trick | Worth lifting? | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 1-second post-kill grace | **yes**, trivial | small patch in `exec_local.go`, cleaner final output |
| `yieldMs` + background sessions + `process` tool | **yes**, big-feature | exactly the missing piece for long-running ops (servers, build watches, agents-in-agents). Largest design lift. |
| PTY mode with fallback | **maybe** | only matters if we want figaro to run TUIs / nested coding agents |
| Two-tier output truncation | **yes** | already a real risk — `find /` would balloon the aria |
| `sanitizeBinaryOutput` | **yes**, trivial | one regex + a code-point filter |
| Streaming `onUpdate` with tail | **partially** — depends on whether the streamWriter UX already exposes this |
| Scoped session registry | falls out of (2) | only relevant once sessions exist |

The headline insight: **openclaw treats "exec" and "background process management" as two cooperating tools, with a session registry between them**. That's the architectural shift; everything else is polish.

I haven't touched the skill — say the word and I'll fold the keepers into `skills.figaro-dev` (or open issues against figaro-qua for the implementation work, whichever fits your flow).
